COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “B” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214, “An Act to Make 9 
Supplemental Appropriations and Allocations for the Expenditures of State Government, 10 
General Fund and Other Funds and to Change Certain Provisions of the Law Necessary to 11 
the Proper Operations of State Government for the Fiscal Years Ending June 30, 2024 and 12 
June 30, 2025” 13 
Amend the bill by inserting after the title and before the enacting clause the following: 14 
'Emergency preamble.  Whereas,  acts and resolves of the Legislature do not 15 
become effective until 90 days after adjournment unless enacted as emergencies; and 16 
Whereas, the 90-day period may not terminate until after the beginning of the next 17 
fiscal year; and 18 
Whereas, certain obligations and expenses incident to the operation of state 19 
departments and institutions will become due and payable immediately; and 20 
Whereas, in the judgment of the Legislature, these facts create an emergency within 21 
the meaning of the Constitution of Maine and require the following legislation as 22 
immediately necessary for the pre servation of the public peace, health and safety; now, 23 
therefore,' 24 
Amend the bill by striking out everything after the enacting clause and inserting the 25 
following: 26 
'PART A 27 
Sec. A-1.  Appropriations and allocations.   The following appropriations and 28 
allocations are made. 29

Initiative: Adjusts funding to align with revenue projections from the March 1, 2024 33 
revenue forecast.34

Sec. C-4. Authorization of payments. If the State's continued obligation for any 14 
individual component contained in those sections of this Part that set the total cost of 15 
funding public education from kindergarten to grade 12 and the local and state 16 
contributions for that purpose exceeds the level of funding provided for that component, 17 
any unexpended balances occurring in other programs may be applied to avoid proration 18 
of payments for any individual component. Any unexpended balances from this Part may 19 
not lapse but must be carried forward for the same purpose.20 
Sec. C-5. Limit of State's obligation. Those sections of this Part that set the total 26 
cost of funding public education from kindergarten to grade 12 and the local and state 27 
contributions for that purpose may not be construed to require the State to provide payments 28 
that exceed the appropriation of funds for general purpose aid for local schools for the fiscal 29 
year beginning July 1, 2024 and ending June 30, 2025. 30

PART E38 
Sec. E-1.  32 MRSA §15224, as amended by PL 2001, c. 573, Pt. B, §28 and affected 8 
by §36, is further amended to read: 9 
§15224.  Installation of new elevators and tramways; fees 10 
Detailed plans or specifications of each new or altered elevator or tramway must be 11 
submitted to and approved by the chief inspector before the construction may be started. 12 
Fees for examination of the plans or specifications must be set by the director under section 13 
15225‑A. For the purposes of this section, fees may not exceed 1.5% of the cost of the new 14 
or altered elevator or tramway. 15 
Sec. E-2.  32 MRSA §15225-A, as amended by PL 2013, c. 70, Pt. D, §28, is further 16 
amended to read: 17 
§15225-A.  Fees 18 
The director may establish by rule fees for purposes authorized under this chapter in 19 
amounts that are reasonable and necessary for their respective purposes, except that the fee 20 
for any one purpose, other than permit and inspection fees and fees set for the purposes of 21 
section 15224, may not exceed $500.  Rules adopted pursuant to this section are routine 22 
technical rules as defined in Title 5, chapter 375, subchapter 2‑A. 23

to adopt rules regarding fees for elevator installation and inspection; report.   25

further amended to read: 37 
2.  Sourcing for sales of tangible personal property and taxable services; generally.  38 
The sale of tangible personal property or a taxable service is sourced in this State pursuant 39 
to this subsection. The provisions of this subsection do not apply to the lease or rental of 40 
tangible personal property or the sale of mobile telecommunications services. 41 
1 
2 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “B” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 150 - 131LR3108(03) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
A.  When the tangible personal property or taxable service is received by the purchaser 1 
at a business location of the seller, the sale is sourced to that business location. 2 
B.  When the tangible personal property or taxable ser vice is not received by the 3 
purchaser at a business location of the seller, the sale is sourced to the location where 4 
receipt by the purchaser or the purchaser's donee occurs, including the location 5 
indicated by instructions for delivery to the purchaser or donee known to the seller. 6 
C.  For a sale when paragraphs A and B do not apply, the sale is sourced to the location 7 
indicated by an address for the purchaser that is available from the business records of 8 
the seller that are maintained in the ordinary course of the seller's business when use of 9 
this address does not constitute bad faith. 10 
D.  For a sale when paragraphs A to C do not apply, the sale is sourced to the location 11 
indicated by an address for the purchaser obtained during the consummation of the 12 
sale, including the address of a purchaser's payment instrument, if no other address is 13 
available, when use of this address does not constitute bad faith. 14 
E.  When paragraphs A to D do not apply, including the circumstance in which the 15 
seller is without su fficient information to apply paragraphs A to D, the location is 16 
determined by the address from which tangible personal property was shipped, from 17 
which the tangible personal property or taxable service transferred electronically was 18 
first available for tr ansmission by the seller or from which the service was provided, 19 
disregarding for these purposes any location that merely provided the digital transfer 20 
of the tangible personal property or taxable service sold. 21 
Sec. H-60.  36 MRSA §1819, sub-§3 is enacted to read: 22 
3.  Sourcing for leases or rentals of tangible personal property.  The lease or rental 23 
of tangible personal property, other than property identified in subsection 4 or 5, is sourced 24 
pursuant to this subsection. 25 
A.  For a lease or renta l that requires recurring periodic payments, the first periodic 26 
payment is sourced to this State in the same manner as a sale of tangible personal 27 
property in accordance with subsection 2.  Periodic payments made subsequent to the 28 
first payment are sourced to the primary property location for each time period covered 29 
by the payment.  For the purposes of this paragraph, "the primary property location" is 30 
an address for the property provided by the lessee that is available to the lessor from 31 
its records and maintained in the ordinary course of business, when use of this address 32

accompanies employees on business trips and service calls.  35

accordance with subsection 2. 38

5-A.  Mass violence crime.  "Mass violence crime" means an intentional violent crime 20

and significantly increases the burdens on victim support and the crime victims' 22 
compensation program. 23 
Sec. N-2.  5 MRSA §3360 -E, as amended by PL 1999, c. 360, §7 and affected by 24

§3360-E.  Payment of awards; limits 27 
Payments from the fund and limits on those payments are governed by this section. 28 
1.  Compensation for victim of sexual assault or other specified crime.  The board 29 
may award compensation to a claimant of up to $15,000 for actual and unreimbursed losses 30 
and eligible expenses of any person who is sexually assaulted or who suffers personal injury 31 
or death as the result of a crime specified in section 3360, subsection 3. 32 
2.  Payment to victim of mass violence crime; source of payments.  Notwithstanding 33 
the compensation limits in subsection 1, if the underlying crime is a mass violence crime, 34 
the board may award a total amount of compensation of more than $15,000.  Any awarded 35 
amount in excess of $15,000 must be paid from the Maine Mass Violence Care Fund 36 
established in section 3360-W. 37 
3.  Award for family or household member.  An award of compensation for the 38 
benefit of a family or household member is derivative of the claim of the victim.  The total 39 
compensation paid from the fund for all claims arising from the crime against the victim 40 
may not exceed $15,000. 41

2 
3 
4

COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
4.  Payment to individuals responsible for medical, funeral and other expenses of 1 
victim.  Within the limits specified in this section, when a person d ies as the direct result 2 
of a specified crime under section 3360, subsection 3, any individual who pays or who is 3 
legally responsible for medical, medically related, funeral or burial expenses may seek 4 
compensation for those unreimbursed expenses incurred by the individual.  A provider of 5

Sec. N-3.  5 MRSA c. 316-D is enacted to read: 12 
CHAPTER 316-D 13 
MAINE MASS VIOLENCE CARE FUND 14 
§3360-W.  Maine Mass Violence Care Fund 15 
1.  Fund established; purpose; source of funds.  The Maine Mass Violence Care 16 
Fund, referred to in this chapter as "the fund," is established within the Department of the 17 
Attorney General as an Other Special Revenue Funds account. The purpose of the fund is 18 
to provide a sustainable source of funds for expenses eligible for reimbursement by the 19 
Victims' Compensation Board established under section 3360 -A arising from a mass 20 
violence crime pursuant to chapter 316 -A that are not paid for by insurance or any other 21 
source. The fund is funded through appropriations and allocations and may receive private 22 
donations and federal and state funds designated by law for the payment of claims and 23 
reasonable administrative costs of the fund. Eligible investment earnings credited to the 24 
assets of the fund become part of the assets of the fund. 25 
2.  Administration and investment of fund. The fund is administered by the Treasurer 26 
of State in accordance with this subsection. 27 
A. In consultation with the Attorney General, the Treasurer of State may hold, invest, 28 
reinvest and manage the fund in a manner that fulfills the purpose of the fund as long 29 
as the investment and reinvestment of funds is in compliance with section 138 and the 30 
Maine Uniform Trust Code, including the Maine Uniform Prudent Investor Act. 31 
B. All costs of administering the fund, including the necessary and proper expenses 32 
incurred by the Treasurer of State in administering the fund, must be paid from the  33 
fund. 34 
C.  The Treasurer of State, the Attorney General and the Victims' Compensation Board 35 
established in section 3360-A may not encumber, invest, divest or disburse funds for 36 
any purpose not specifically included in this section. 37 
3.  Distributions from fund.  The Victims' Compensation Board established under 38 
section 3360-A shall make distributions from the fund in accordance with chapter 316 -A 39 
and rules establishing eligibility criteria adopted by the board. 40 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “B” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 157 - 131LR3108(03) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
A.   Only gains, interest, dividends and other revenue earned on funds in the fund and 1 
any amounts gifted to the fund may be expended. 2 
B. Payments from the fund to a victim for eligible expenses, as set forth in section 3 
3360-E, may not be made sooner than 3 years after the applicable mass violence crime. 4 
4.  Rules. The board may adopt rules to implement the provisions of this section 5 
including establishing eligibility criteria. 6 
5.  Annual report. The Attorney General and the Treasurer of State shall report to the 7 
joint standing committee of the Legislature having jurisdiction over judiciary matters by 8 
February 1st of each year regarding implementation of the fund, including procedures 9 
developed by the Victims' Compensation Board, total revenue available for reimbursement 10 
of eligible claims and annual expenditures from the fund. 11 
Sec. N-4.  Working group on Maine Mass Violence Care Fund.  The Working 12 
Group to Recommend any Changes to Eligibility Standards for Expenditures from the 13 
Maine Mass Violence Care Fund, referred to in this section as "the working group," is 14 
established. 15 
1. Definitions.  As used in this section, unless the context o therwise indicates, the 16 
following terms have the following meanings.  17 
A. "Board" means the Victims' Compensation Board established in the Maine Revised 18 
Statutes, Title 5, section 3360-A.  19 
B. "Eligible expenses" means expenses that are determined by the board to be eligible 20 
for reimbursement from the fund as of May 1, 2024.  21 
C. "Family or household member" has the same meaning as in the Maine Revised 22 
Statutes, Title 5, section 3360, subsection 5. 23 
D. "Mass violence crime" means an intentional violent crime th at results in physical, 24 
emotional or psychological injury to a large number of individuals and that 25 
significantly increases the burdens on victim support and compensation systems in the 26 
jurisdiction in which the violent crime occurred.  27 
E. "Victim" has the  same meaning as in the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 5, section 28 
200-E, subsection 1, paragraph B. 29 
2. Purpose of working group.  The purpose of the working group is to identify and 30 
recommend to the board and the Legislature  any changes regarding specific op tions and 31 
eligibility criteria to help ensure that those individuals adversely affected by a mass 32 
violence crime are provided some financial relief from physical and behavioral health care 33 
costs not paid for from another public or private source, including , but not limited to, the 34 
MaineCare program, Medicaid or private insurance.  Specifically, the working group shall 35 
consider and make recommendations regarding: 36 
A. Gaps in payments for physical and behavioral health care services for victims of 37 
mass violence crimes; 38 
B. Methods of investing the funds in the fund to ensure sustainable annual financial 39 
returns;  40 
C. Options for determining eligi bility for distributions from the fund, including any 41 
changes regarding parameters for:  42 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “B” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214

COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
(1) Who is considered a victim of a mass violence crime;  1 
(2) Which health care costs are considered eligible expenses; and 2 
(3) What constitutes a mass violence crime; and  3 
D. Anything else the working group determines necessary to carry out the purposes of 4 
the fund.  5 
3. Membership; chair; appointments. The working group consists of the following 6 
members:  7 
A. A member of the Senate, appointed by the President of the Senate;  8 
B. A member of the House of Representatives, appointed by the Speaker of the House;  9 
C. The Attorney General or the Attorney General's designee;  10 
D. The Commissioner of Health and Human Services or the commissioner's designee;  11 
E. The Treasurer of State or the Treasurer of State's designee; and  12 
F. The chair of the board or the chair's designee. 13 
The member of the Senate and the member of the House of Representatives serve as 14 
cochairs.  15 
All appointments must be made within 30 days following the effective date of this Part. 16 
4. Report. The working group under subsection 2 shall provide its recommendations 17

working group shall r eport to the Victims’ Compensation Board and the joint standing 19

2024. The joint standing comm ittee of the Legislature having jurisdiction over judiciary 22

PART T 5 
Sec. T-1. Department of Public Safety to establish public safety health and 6 
wellness grant pilot program.    The Department of Public Safety shall establish a 7 
2-year public safety health and wellness grant pilot program, referred to in this Part as "the 8 
pilot program," to provide grants to government entities for the purpose of providing public 9 
safety employees with wellness visits or specialized cardiac and metabolic screenings that 10 
specifically address the physical or mental health effects experienced by public safety 11 
employees.  Services provided under the pilot program may not supplant existing 12 
behavioral, mental or physical health care benefit packages and must supplement existing 13 
programs.  For the purposes of this Part, the following terms have the following meanings. 14 
1.  "Government entity" means the State or a municipality, plantation or county. 15 
2.  "Public safety agency" means a department or other agency of a government entity 16 
that provides or has the authority to provide fire, emergency medical, emergency 17 
communications, correctional or police services. 18 
3.  "Public safety employee" means an employee of a public safety agency. 19 
Sec. T -2. Programs to address physical and mental health effects 20 
experienced by public safety employees.   A government entity may apply for a grant 21 
under the pilot program for any group of public safety employees as long as services are 22 
provided to all public safety employees of the public safety agency within that group, 23 
wherever located.  Applications by a government entity must include at least one of the 2 24 
following screening programs: 25 
1.  Specialized cardiac and metabolic screening that provides a medical consultation 26 
and an individualized plan including nutrition, fitness and wellness recommendations to 27 
the employee when appropriate.  The results of the screening and any advice for t he 28 
continued treatment of identified health issues must be provided to the employee and the 29 
employee's physician.  Testing must include the following: 30 
A.  An advanced lipid panel, including a cardiac inflammatory biomarker analysis; 31 
B.  Screening for liver and kidney function; 32 
C.  Screening for thyroid, prostate and other cancers or diseases that are prevalent 33 
among first responders at a higher rate than the civilian population, such as diabetes; and 34 
D.  Cardiologist-guided, public safety-specific, cardio-metabolic stress testing; and 35 
2.  Annual wellness visits that provide confidential visits with qualified mental health 36 
professionals who have experience with the cumulative impact of exposure to traumatic 37 
events and specialized knowledge of public safety ps ychology.  Options for referrals to 38 
additional counseling services, inpatient services or specialists for the participating 39 
employee or employee's immediate family must be available.    40 
Unless otherwise provided by law, services provided under this section may not be 41 
used as a basis for employment termination. 42 
1 
2 
3 
4 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “B” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 161 - 131LR3108(03) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
Sec. T -3. Confidentiality.   All health care information of an employe e is 1 
confidential as provided in the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 22, section 1711 -C.  If 2 
wellness visits are mandated as a condition of employment by a public safety agency, only 3 
confirmation of attendance may be shared by a health care provider with the agency. 4 
Sec. T-4. Administration costs.  A government entity that receives a grant under 5 
the pilot program may use up to 10% of the grant funding to administer the grant. 6 
Sec. T-5. Reporting.  The Department of Public Safety shall ensure that government 7 
entities receiving grants provide to the department detailed anonymized information on the 8 
number of public safety employees who participated in the pilot program, the types of 9 
services provided to those employees and any outcome data that can be provided t o show 10 
effectiveness of the pilot program.  The Department of Public Safety shall submit a report 11 
no later than January 10, 2026 to the joint standing committee of the Legislature having 12 
jurisdiction over health and human services matters and the joint standing committee of the 13 
Legislature having jurisdiction over criminal justice and public safety matters with the 14 
number of grants disbursed, the number of public safety employees served, the types of 15 
services provided and outcome data on the effectiveness of the program. 16

Sec. W-17.  20-A MRSA §7209-A is enacted to read: 10 
§7209-A.  Transition of responsibility for en suring a free, appropriate public 11 
education for children eligible under Part B, Section 619 12 
In order to meet the requirement that, beginning July 1, 2028, all school administrative 13 
units are designated as responsible for child find activities and for ensur ing a free, 14 
appropriate public education for children eligible under Part B, Section 619 pursuant to 15 
section 7006, the following transition schedule and supports apply. 16 
1. Transition year one.  Beginning July 1, 2024, school administrative units may be 17 
approved by the commissioner to assume the responsibility for child find activities and for 18 
ensuring a free, appropriate public education for children eligible under Part B, Section 19 
619. The depar tment shall approve readiness plans in accordance with subsection 8 and 20 
shall provide professional learning in working with young children and their families and 21 
technical support throughout the planning and implementation of the first year to assist 22 
school administrative units to prepare to meet the standards of the readiness plans. Funding 23 
must be provided to school administrative units on a quarterly basis in accordance with 24 
section 7303. Prior to a school administrative unit assuming responsibilities for child find 25 
activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education, the department shall 26 
establish a memorandum of understanding with the school administrative unit to determine 27 
the services to be provided by the department and the regional supp ort and service hub. 28 
The memorandum of understanding must be reviewed and updated in response to 29 
unanticipated needs each month.  The department shall contract with a national expert to 30 
regularly monitor funding and programming and recommend changes to be considered as 31 
part of the transition year one activities.  32 
2. Additional transition years.  During the 2025 -2026, 2026 -2027 and 2027 -2028 33 
school years, the commissioner shall approve school administrative units in addition to 34 
those approved under subsection 1 to assume responsibility for child find activities and for 35 
ensuring a free, appropriate public education. The department shall provide professional 36 
learning, funding and technical assistance in the same manner as provided to school 37 
administrative units in subsection 1.  38 
3. Additional time for certain school administrative units.  If the commissioner 39 
determines that a school administrative unit is not able to assume responsibility for child 40 
find activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education by July 1, 2028 because 41 
the school administrative unit requires additional time and support in regions where related 42 
services and staffing are not available to support the transition, the commissioner shall 43 
provide that school administrative unit with necessary resources and an additional year to 44 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “B” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 167 - 131LR3108(03) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
assume responsibility for child find activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public 45 
education. If the school administrative unit cannot assume responsibility for child find 46 
activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education, as determined by the 47 
commissioner, the school administrative unit may qualify for a modified plan for managing 48 
children eligible under Part B, Section 619 in accordance with section 7006, subsection 4.49

child find activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education.  43

only partially been provided, the Child Development Services System shall schedule an 45

§7211.  Regional support and service hubs 13 
The Child Development Services System shall establish 9 regional support and service 14 
hubs that are aligned with each of the 9 superintendent regions established by the statewide 15 
association of superi ntendents. The regional support and service hubs shall provide 16 
supports and resources to school administrative units that have assumed the responsibility 17 
for child find activities and for providing a free, appropriate public education to children 18 
eligible under Part B, Section 619 pursuant to section 7006, subsection 2 and other high -19 
quality early childhood programs partnering with or otherwise contracted by a school 20 
administrative unit to fulfill the school administrative unit's responsibilities under Part  B, 21 
Section 619 pursuant to section 7006, subsection 2 as determined through memoranda of 22 
understanding between the department and the school administrative unit.  23 
1. Minimum requirements. Each regional support and service hub shall, at a 24 
minimum, offer th e following supports, assistance and resources to the school 25 
administrative units within the superintendent region to which the regional support and 26 
service hub is aligned: 27 
A.  Assistance with child find activities; 28 
B. Training and other professional development opportunities and technical assistance 29 
with the implementation of developmentally appropriate practices for young children, 30 
including, but not limited to, curriculum, screening and assessment selections aligned 31 
with the State's early learning d evelopmental standards, understanding of and 32 
requirements to meet free, appropriate public education and least restrictive 33 
environment standards and best practices for inclusive learning; 34 
C. Assistance with establishing and strengthening community partners hips with 35 
existing inclusive, high-quality early childhood programs to help school administrative 36 
units meet federal obligations under Part B, Section 619. High-quality early childhood 37 
programs include, but are not limited to, Head Start programs, private prekindergarten 38 
and child care programs and other community-based programs; 39 
D. Assistance with locating transportation services; 40 
E. Assistance with administrative tasks associated with the assumption of 41 
responsibility for a free, appropriate public education under Part B, Section 619; and 42 
F. Maintenance and coordination of access to credentialed educators and service 43 
providers who are avail able to school administrative units on a contractual basis, 44

Sec. W-19.  20-A MRSA §7303 is enacted to read: 31 
§7303.  Per-pupil rate for children eligible under Part B, Section 619 32 
Funding for school administrative units that assume responsibility for child find 33 
activities and for ensuring a free, appropriate public education for children eligible under 34 
Part B, Section 619 pursuant to section 7006, subsection 2 may not be appropr iated to or 35

eligible under Part B, Section 619 must be calculated on a per -pupil basis in the same 39 
manner by which operating allocations are generated in sections 15674, 15675 and 15681.  40 
2. Preschool special education and related services allocation. The preschool special 41 
education and related services per-pupil allocation must be calculated annually for children 42

eligible under Part B, Section 619 at the EPS per-pupil rate for each school administrative 43

Sec. DD-2.  5 MRSA c. 310-B is enacted to read: 16 
CHAPTER 310-B 17 
MAINE OFFICE OF COMMUNITY AFFAIRS 18 
§3201.  Definitions 19 
As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise indicates, the following terms 20 
have the following meanings.  21 
1.  Director.   "Director" means the Director of the Maine Office of Community Affairs 22 
appointed pursuant to section 3203. 23 
2.  Office.    "Office" means the Maine Office of Commu nity Affairs established by 24 
section 3202. 25 
§3202.  Office established; purpose 26 
The Maine Office of Community Affairs is established as an agency in the executive 27 
branch to foster communications and partnerships between the State and communities in 28 
this State. The office shall engage with municipalities, tribal governments and regional 29 
councils to provide coordinated and efficient planning, technical assistance and financial 30 
support to better plan for challenges, pursue solutions and create stronger, more res ilient 31 
communities. 32 
The office is established to partner with communities in this State and regional councils 33 
by: 34 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “B” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 176 - 131LR3108(03) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
1. Assistance  and fund ing. Providing technical assistance and funding related to 1 
planning to municipalities, tribal governments and regional councils that supports a 2 
sustainable future for the State's people, communities, natural resources, physical 3 
infrastructure, industries, businesses and institutions; and 4 
2. Coordination and communication. Facilitating general coordination and 5 
communication between municipalities, tribal governments, regional councils and State 6 
Government. 7 
§3203.  Director 8 
The Director of the Maine Office of Community Affairs is appointed by the Governor 9 
and serves at the pleasure of the Governor.  The director must have demonstrated 10 
experience and leadership in municipal or regional government and must bring expertise 11 
in planning, technical assistance and grant programs for communities. 12 
§3204.  Powers and duties 13 
The director shall exercise the powers of the office and is responsible for the execution 14 
of the duties of the office. 15 
1.  Duties of director.  The director shall: 16 
A.  Appoint and remove office staff and prescribe staff duties as necessary to 17 
implement the duties of the office, including: 18 
(1)  Hiring professional staff that have education, training and experience in the 19 
fields of planning and development, local and regional government, climate 20 
science and resilience, housing, building codes and general policy making; and 21 
(2)  Employing additional staff as necessary to support the work of the office; 22 
B.  Supervise and administer the affairs of the office and advise the Governor and other 23 
officials of State Government on matters of communication and partnerships between 24 
the State, municipalities, tribal governments and regional councils in this State; 25 
C.  At the request of the Governor, act for the State in the initiation of or participation 26 
in any multigovernmental agency program related to the purposes of the office; 27 
D.  At the request of the Governor, prepare and submit a budget for the office; and 28 
E. At the request of the Governor, report on the activities of the office and, after 29 
consultation with and approval by the Governor, submit recommendations for 30 
legislative action as are determined necessary to further the purposes of this chapter. 31 
2.  Duties of office.  Under the supervision of the director, the office shall: 32 
A.  Provide technical assistance an d resources to municipalities, tribal governments 33 
and regional councils on issues related to planning, climate resilience and development; 34 
B.  Collect and collate data and statistics relating to the issues described in paragraph 35 
A and provide them to municipalities, tribal governments and regional councils; 36 
C.  Assist municipalities, tribal governments and regional councils, as well as the State, 37 
in applying for, using and leveraging federal funding resources on issues of importance 38 
to communities and the State; 39 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “B” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 177 - 131LR3108(03) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
D.  Make grants from money appropriated to the office by the Legislature and any 1 
funds received by the office for the purposes of the office, including federal funding or 2 
private funds; solicit applications for grants; and make grant awards to eligible 3 
communities and to service provider organizations as determined by the office, 4 
including establishing eligibility requirements and ot her criteria to consider in 5 
awarding grants; 6 
E. Administer contracts with regional councils and regional planning and development 7

§3205.  Acceptance and administration of funds 25 
The office may accept, administer and expend funds, including but not limited to funds 26 
from the Federal Government or f rom private sources, for purposes consistent with this 27 
chapter.  The director shall provide a report of the amount of any outside funding received 28 
from private sources and its designated purpose to the Governor and the joint standing 29 
committee of the Legislature having jurisdiction over municipal matters on an annual basis. 30 
§3206.  Contracts; agreements 31 
The office may employ expert and professional consultants, contract for services as the 32 
director determines necessary within the limits of the funds provide d and consistent with 33 
the powers and duties of the office and enter into agreements with the Federal Government 34 
and other agencies and organizations that promote the objectives of this chapter. 35

§1730.  Upper payment limits for aggregate MaineCare payments to hospitals 33 
1. Definitions. As used in this section, the following terms have the following 34

Page 182 - 131LR3108(03) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
2. Department to ensure compliance with upper payment limits. Beginning July 1, 1 
2024, if aggregate MaineCare  payments made to a group of hospitals exceed the upper 2 
payment limit applicable to that group of hospitals under 42 Code of Federal Regulations, 3 
Section 447.272 or 447.321, the department shall limit payments to that group of hospitals 4 
to the level that e nsures compliance with the applicable upper payment limit. At least 60 5 
days prior to taking an action pursuant to this subsection, the department shall share its 6 
upper payment calculations, including all data inputs, with the hospitals affected by the 7 
action.  8 
3. Adjustments when aggregate payments fall below upper payment limits. If the 9 
department limits MaineCare payments to a group of hospitals pursuant to subsection 2 and 10 
the Federal Government subsequently determines that the payments made to the group  of 11 
hospitals are below the upper payment limit applicable to that group of hospitals under 42 12 
Code of Federal Regulations, Section 447.272 or 447.321, the department shall increase 13 
the payments to an amount determined by the department, as permitted under  federal 14 
regulations, and not higher than the applicable upper payment limit. The department shall 15 
notify the affected hospitals of any payments made under this subsection. 16

Sec. ZZ-1.  26 MRSA §632-A is enacted to read: 26 
§632-A.  Fund for recovered wages 27 
1. Fund established. The Wage Recovery Fund is established as a nonlapsing fund 28 
within the bureau.  The purpose of the fund is to facilitate payments related to unpaid 29 
wages, unpaid health benefits, liquidated damages or interest owed to employees or former 30 
employees of an employer when the Department of Labor receives payments from an 31 
employer in accordance with a settlement agreement or a judgment on behalf of affected 32 
employees or former employees. 33 
2. Administration. The fund is administered by the director. Payment of unpaid wages, 34 
unpaid health benefits, liquidated damages or interest to affected individuals may be made 35 
only to the extent that the Department of Labor receives payment from the employer in 36 
accordance with a settlement agreement or a judgment.  Th e department is not liable for 37 
payments to affected individuals if the department does not receive the funds from the 38 
employer. 39 
3. Educ ation. As part of its settlement agreements, the Department of Labor may 40 
include a provision for payment of funds toward education and public messaging regarding 41 
the State's labor laws. Funds deposited in the Wage Recovery Fund that are not required 42

Office of the State Fire Marshal in a Fire Investigator position may be promoted to a Senior 11 
Fire Investigator position if that person becomes certified as a Certified Fire Investigator 12 
by the International Association of Arson Investigators or equivalent certific ation body. 13 
The effective date of the promotion is the date the employee officially becomes certified. 14 
When a Senior Fire Investigator position is vacated, that position reverts to a Fire 15 
Investigator position. 16

General Fund due to section 1 of this Part must be provided from the Salary Plan program, 18 
General Fund account in the Department of Administrative and Financial Services in an 19 
amount up to $10,000 for the fiscal year ending Ju ne 30, 2024 and in an amount up to 20 
$13,000 for the fiscal year ending June 30, 2025. 21

§3613.  Crisis receiving centers 42 
1

1.  Definition.  As used in this section, unless the context otherwise indicates, "crisis 1 
receiving center" means a center that provides immediate and short-term walk-in access to 2 
an array of both clinical and nonclinical mental health and substance use disorder crisis 3 
stabilization services to all individuals seeking care regardless of acuity or insurance 4 
coverage and within bounds of licensing. 5 
2.  Authority. The department shall develop a plan for a network of community-based 6 
crisis receiving centers across the State to support both clinical and nonclinical mental 7 
health and substance use disorder crisis stabilization services. The department shall also 8 
coordinate meetings, technical assistance and training and provide other assistance to help 9 
create, maintain and, as necessary, expand the network. 10 
3.  Guidelines.  The department shall: 11 
A. Consult with law enforcement agencies, municipalities, public health experts, 12 
behavioral health care providers, other states and others as appropriate; 13 
B. Assess geographical locations for maximization of community impact; 14 
C. Provide technical assistance to persons and entities across the State and providers 15 
interested in joining the network; 16 
D. Coordinate regular meetings with crisis receiving centers and provide technical 17 
assistance to crisis receiving centers; and 18 
E. Engage in continual process improvement and planning updates. 19

PART SSS 14 
Sec. SSS-1.  22 MRSA §1708-A is enacted to read: 15 
§1708-A.  Compensation to Maine Veterans' Homes 16 
Services provided by a veterans' facility must be reimbursed by the MaineCare program 17 
at rates established by the department  pursuant to this section.  This section applies to all 18 
funds, including federal funds, paid by an agency of the State to a veterans' facility for 19 
resident care. For the purposes of this section, "veterans' facility" means a nursing facility, 20 
a residential care facility or a multilevel health care facility that is operated by the Maine 21 
Veterans' Homes at any location required under Title 37-B, section 601, subsection 2. 22 
1.  Per resident basis.  Veterans' facilities must be reimbursed on a per resident daily 23 
rate basis for services to residents covered under the MaineCare program.  Different rates 24 
may be established for services equivalent to those provided by nursing homes as defined 25 
in section 1812-A, residential care facilities as defined in section 7852, subsection 14 and 26 
multilevel health care facilities as defined in section 7852, subsection 10-A. 27 
2.  Rate calculations.   Rate calculations under this section must result in 28 
reimbursement of the portion of the total MaineCare allowable cost of operating each 29 
veterans' facility attributable to the provision of services to residents who receive 30 
MaineCare benefits.  Different rates may be established for services equivalent to those 31 
provided by nursing homes as defined in section 1812 -A, residential care facilities as 32 
defined in section 7852, subsection 14 and multilevel health care facilities as defined in 33 
section 7852, subsection 10-A. 34 
3.  Annual adjustments for inflation.  Rates established pursuant to this section must 35 
be adjusted annually to reflect projected inflation for the year to which the rates will apply. 36 
4.  Calculation of per resident daily rate; limitation.  The department may use data 37 
from other states' veterans' home programs and appropriate price indices to establish the 38 
rates required in this section, as long as the application of data from other states' veterans' 39 
home programs and price indices does not reduce reimbursement below the portion of the 40 
total MaineCare allowable cost as described in subsection 2. 41 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “B” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 192 - 131LR3108(03) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
5.  Use of 3rd party.  The department may contract with a 3rd party to derive or review 1 
the rates established under this section. 2

PART XXX 17 
Sec. XXX -1.  Prospective payment system hospital transition plans.  The 18 
Department of Health and Human Services shall work with any hospital that is reimbursed 19 
by the federal Medicare program as a prospe ctive payment system hospital and that was 20 
reimbursed by the MaineCare program as a critical access hospital for outpatient services 21 
on or before January 1, 2024 to determine a plan for transitioning to reimbursement by the 22 
MaineCare program as a prospective payment system hospital while maintaining financial 23 
solvency. This transition plan may include but is not limited to ways in which the hospital 24 
can expand services or reduce expenses. Any hospital that is reimbursed by the federal 25 
Medicare program as a prospective payment system hospital and is reimbursed by the 26 
MaineCare program as a critical access hospital for outpatient services shall pursue federal 27 
and state provisions and programs that would improve its financial position, including but 28 
not limited  to wage reclassification by the Medicare Geographic Classification Review 29 
Board. As part of the transition plan, the department shall work with any hospital eligible 30 
under this section to determine the amount of a transitional supplemental payment based 31 
on calendar year 2022 cost reports. By March 31, 2029, the department shall submit to the 32 
joint standing committee of the Legislature having jurisdiction over health and human 33 
services matters a report on any transition plans developed under this section. 34

Sec. DDDD -1. Strengthen and expand mental health crisis intervention 12 
mobile response services.   The Department of Health and Human Services shall 13 
strengthen and expand mental health crisis intervention mobile response services in order 14 
to provide services 24 hours a day, 7 days a week.  The department shall provide for the 15 
incorporation of mobile outreach peer support specialists, certified intentional peer support 16 
specialists and recovery coaches, mental h ealth law enforcement liaisons through 17 
behavioral health agencies and community debriefing and critical incident response 18 
services into the existing crisis services response system.  The department shall also provide 19 
for ancillary services that are require d components of mental health crisis intervention 20 
mobile response services.  The funding for these ancillary services must include travel costs 21 
to and from mobile face -to-face assessments not to exceed the federal per mile rate, 22 
reimbursement for travel ti me to and from mobile face -to-face assessments and 23 
reimbursement for time spent on telephone conferences with clients.  The department shall 24 
provide reimbursement for peer support services provided as mental health crisis 25 
intervention mobile response services under the MaineCare program. 26 
Sec. DDDD -2. E-9-1-1 and 9 -8-8 coordination.   By January 30, 2025, the 27 
Department of Health and Human Services, in coordination with the Public Utilities 28 
Commission, Emergency Services Communication Bureau and the Departmen t of Public 29 
Safety, shall ensure the coordination of services under the State's E -9-1-1 system and the 30 
State's 9-8-8 mobile crisis services system.  By January 30, 2026, the Department of Health 31 
and Human Services shall submit a status report related to th e coordination of services, 32 
including suggested legislation, to the joint standing committee of the Legislature having 33 
jurisdiction over health and human services matters and to the joint standing committee of 34 
the Legislature having jurisdiction over utili ties matters.  The joint standing committees 35 
may each submit a bill relating to the report to the Second Regular Session of the 132nd 36 
Legislature. 37

PART EEEE 12 
Sec. EEEE-1.  34-B MRSA §3613 is enacted to read: 13 
§3613.  Crisis receiving centers 14 
1. Definitions.  As used in this section, unless the context otherwise indicates, the 15 
following terms have the following meanings. 16 
A.  "Crisis receiving center" means a center providing walk-in access to crisis services 17 
to individuals experiencing behavioral health, mental health and substance use 18 
challenges. 19 
B.  "Culturally sensitive trauma -informed care" means care that acknowledges, 20 
respects and integrates the cultural values, beliefs and practices of  individuals and 21 
families. 22 
2.  Crisis receiving centers.  The department shall establish 2 crisis receiving centers 23 
to support individuals dealing with behavioral health, mental health or substance use issues.  24 
The receiving centers must be established in Aroostook County and Penobscot County.  25 
The department shall ensure that the crisis receiving centers provide culturally sensitive 26 
trauma-informed care.  The department shall develop a plan to expand crisis receiving 27 
centers statewide, with at least one cr isis receiving center located in each county of the 28 
State. 29 
3.  Rules.  The department may adopt rules to implement this section.  Rules adopted 30 
pursuant to this subsection are routine technical rules as defined in Title 5, chapter 375, 31 
subchapter 2-A. 32

Title 5, section 3360 -A; the Department of Education; the Office of Behavioral Health 4 
established under Title 5, section 20011; the Office of the Atto rney General; the 5 
Department of Public Safety; the Maine Bureau of Veterans' Services established under 6 
Title 37-B, section 501; and the violence prevention program within the department. 7 
4.  Awareness and education.  The office shall increase the awareness of and educate 8 
the general public about laws and resources relating to violence prevention and conduct 9 
awareness and education campaigns in accordance with this subsection. 10 
A.  The office shall increase the awareness of and educate the general public about state 11 
and federal laws and existing resources relating to violence prevention, including: 12 
(1)  The availability of and the process for requesting protection orders, including, 13 
but not limited to, protection from abuse orders under Title 19-A, chapter 103 and 14 
protection from harassment orders under Title 5, chapter 337-A; 15 
(2)  The process for accessing available mental health and substance use disorder 16 
resources and how to refer individuals to needed mental health and substance use 17 
disorder treatment services, including suicide prevention services; 18 
(3)  The process for accessing available resources and services for domestic 19 
violence prevention; 20 
(4)  The process for reporting a lost or stolen firearm, including reporting 21 
requirements in state law; 22 
(5)  The best practices for safe storage of firearms; and 23 
(6)  Safe and responsible gun ownership, including increased awareness of the law 24 
and methods of compliance with state and federal law. 25 
B.  The office shall conduct awareness and education campaigns and deve lop and 26 
provide educational materials and training resources, including: 27 
(1)  Developing and providing educational materials and training resources to local 28 
law enforcement agencies, health care providers and educators to assist those 29 
agencies, providers a nd educators with educating the public about the laws, 30 
available resources and effective violence prevention strategies; 31 
(2)  Conducting awareness and education campaigns in a culturally competent way, 32 
including by providing materials and resources in multiple languages;   33 
(3)  Conducting awareness and education campaigns directed toward gun owners, 34 
parents and legal guardians of children and organizations that provide services to 35 
individuals and communities disproportionately affected by gun violence; and 36 
(4)  At the request of the Director of the Maine Center for Disease Control and 37 
Prevention, supporting and providing assistance for education campaigns and 38 
programs conducted by the department that are related to gun violence, including 39 
education campaigns and programs relating to the safe storage of firearms and 40 
suicide prevention. 41 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “B” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 200 - 131LR3108(03) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
The office may focus the awareness and education cam paigns required under this 1 
paragraph in communities identified by the office as disproportionately affected by gun 2 
violence and use television messaging, radio broadcasts, print media, digital strategies 3 
or any other form of messaging considered effective and appropriate by the office to 4 
achieve the goals of this section. 5 
5.  Grant program.   Subject to available funding, the office may establish and 6 
administer a grant program to award grants to organizations to conduct community -based 7 
violence intervention initiatives that are primarily focused on interrupting cycles of 8 
violence, including gun violence, trauma and retaliation by providing culturally competent 9 
intervention services. 10 
A.  To be eligible for a grant award, an organization must demonstrate the ab ility to 11 
conduct effective community -based violence intervention initiatives that meet the 12 
criteria described in this subsection and in rules adopted by the Maine Center for 13 
Disease Control and Prevention. The office shall prioritize awarding grants to 14 
organizations that conduct violence intervention initiatives with individuals and in 15 
communities identified as having the highest imminent risk of perpetrating or being 16 
victimized by violence. 17 
B.  An initiative conducted with a grant award must use strategies  that are evidence-18 
informed and have demonstrated potential for reducing violence without contributing 19 
to mass incarceration, such as group violence interventions, evidence-based street and 20 
community outreach programs, violence interruption and crisis management programs 21 
and individualized wraparound services. To improve the effectiveness of a violence 22 
intervention initiative, a grant recipient shall conduct regular evaluations of the 23 
initiative, including community input and engagement. 24 
C.  The Maine Center for Disease Control and Prevention shall adopt rules necessary 25 
for the administration of the grant program, including grant application procedures, 26 
criteria for determining the amount and duration of the grants and reporting 27 
requirements for organizations that receive grants. 28 
D.  In administering the grant program, the office shall collaborate with stakeholders 29 
as needed to ensure equity in the distribution of grants.  The office shall consult with 30 
stakeholders to develop grant priorities. Stakeholders mu st include individuals and 31 
families affected by violence, organizations with expertise in violence prevention and 32 
gun safety and representatives of communities of color. 33 
E.  By February 1, 2027, the department shall submit to the joint standing committee 34 
of the Legislature having jurisdiction over health and human services matters a report 35 
that includes the following: 36 
(1)  Information regarding the number of grants awarded and the amount of funding 37 
provided to each grant recipient; 38 
(2)  A description of violence intervention initiatives funded, including the number 39 
of individuals served and the communities served by each funded initiative; and 40 
(3)  Recommendations regarding the continuation of the grant program and 41 
recommendations for any changes to the program. 42 
F.  This subsection is repealed June 30, 2027. 43

6.  Data hub.  The office shall create and maintain a data hub of regularly updated and 1 
accurate materials and resources as a repository for data, research and statistical 2 
information regarding violence in the State, including gun violence. As part of maintaining 3 
the data hub, the office shall: 4 
A.  Assist researchers who are seeking information regarding violence in the State; 5 
B.  Collaborate with researchers, including organizations that conduct gun violence 6 
research, to: 7 
(1)  Identify gaps in available data needed to conduct violence prevention research 8 
and develop strategies to improve relevant data collection in the State; 9 
(2)  Use existing available research to enhance evidence-based violence prevention 10 
tools and resources available to communities in the State; and 11 
(3)  Improve the understanding of the disproportionate barriers to safe ty from 12 
violence by encouraging disaggregation of data by race and ethnicity when 13 
research is conducted; and 14 
C.  Promote new and relevant research regarding violence prevention and, if possible, 15 
make the research accessible to researchers and the public. 16 
7.  Reporting requirements.   The office and the department shall provide the 17 
following reports relating to the office's work. 18 
A.  Annually, by November 30th, the office shall report to the department on the 19 
activities it has conducted in the preceding 12 months. The report must include: 20 
(1)  Information regarding awareness and education campaigns conducted by the 21 
office; 22 
(2)  Effective violence intervention programs identified by the office; 23 
(3)  Any federal grants or other funding the office applied for an d whether the 24 
office received those grants or other funds; 25 
(4)  A general summary of new and relevant research included in the office's data 26 
hub under subsection 6 and the nature of research assistance provided by the office; 27 
and 28 
(5)  Recommendations to en hance the administration and operation of the office 29 
and improve the availability of services to reduce violence in the State. 30 
The office shall make the report available on its publicly accessible website or on the 31 
Maine Center for Disease Control and Prevention's publicly accessible website.   32 
B.  In its annual report to the joint standing committee of the Legislature having 33 
jurisdiction over health and human services matters pursuant to section 1425, the 34 
Maine Center for Disease Control and Prevention shall include a summary of the 35 
office's annual report submitted under paragraph A, including recommendations under 36 
paragraph A, subparagrap h (5) and instructions for accessing any new and relevant 37 
violence prevention research identified by the office in paragraph A, subparagraph (4). 38 
The Maine Center for Disease Control and Prevention shall make the summary 39 
available on its publicly accessible website. 40

B.  "Department" means the Department of Public Safety. 1

2.  Administration of gun shop project.  The department shall administer a gun shop 7 
project. 8 
3.  Development and creation of educational materi als; online training .  In 9 
administering a gun shop project under this section, the department shall contract with a 10 
statewide organization with expertise in mental health for the development and creation of 11 
suicide prevention educational materials, including an online training course. 12 
A.  Educational materials under this subsection must include but are not limited to 13 
information on: 14 
(1)  Understanding and recognizing the various clinical signs, symptoms and 15 
indicators of suicide risk; and 16 
(2)  Available suicide prevention resources. 17

contracted statewide organization must refer to the following: 19 
(1)  Gun shop projects in other states; 20 
(2)  Programs created or offered by organizati ons in the dangerous or deadly 21 
weapon industry; and 22 
(3)  Other projects or organizations that the department determines appropriate. 23 
C.  Educational materials under this subsection must be created as written materials, 24 
such as pamphlets, signs, posters, ti p sheets or other media, and as an online training 25 
course for firearm dealers licensed as dealers under 18 United States Code, Section 26 
923(a)(3) and gun shop customers. 27 
4.  Distribution of gun shop project educational materials.   The department shall 28 
ensure that the written educational materials and online training course created under 29 
subsection 3 are available on the department's publicly accessible website. 30

PART WWWW 10 
Sec. WWWW-1.  22 MRSA §3174-OOO is enacted to read: 11 
§3174-OOO.  Reimbursement for treatment of personality disorder and emotional 12 
dysregulation 13 
Beginning January 1, 2025, the department shall reimburse under the MaineCare 14 
program for the treatment of personality disorder and other disorders associated with 15 
primary emotional dysregulation.  In accordance with principles and processes articulated 16 
in section 3173 -J, subsection 2, the department shall establish a bundled reimbursement 17 
rate for the evidence -based treatment of MaineCare members diagnosed with personality 18 
disorder or other disorders associated with pri mary emotional dysregulation.  In 19 
establishing the bundled reimbursement rate, the department shall consider various bundled 20 
reimbursement rate structures, including a daily rate and a monthly rate. The bundled 21 
reimbursement rate must include participation  in a dialectical behavior therapy intensive 22 
outpatient program, psychiatry services, nursing services, case management, residential 23 
services, after-hours skills coaching and supported employment services. 24

PART XXXX 26 
Sec. XXXX-1.  34-B MRSA §1228 is enacted to read: 27 
§1228.  Contingency fund 28 
The department shall establish and maintain a contingency fund, referred to in this 29 
section as "the fund," to provide supplemental assistance for children and adults with severe 30 
behavioral health diagnoses when those needs are not met by other state or federal 31 
programs.  The fund is nonlapsing and must be used to supplement, not supplant, other 32 
expenditures by the department to assist children and adults with severe behavioral health 33 
diagnoses. 34 
1.  Funds.  Money in the fund may be used by the department to assist a child or adult 35 
with a severe behavioral health diagnosis in the following ways: 36 
A.  To support enhanced reimbursement rates or additional staffing needs in the child's 37 
or adult's home or community; 38 
B.  To fund physical accommodations that ensure the child's or adult's home is safe; or 39 
C.  To address other needs identified by the child's or adult's family or providers of 40 
services that are necessary to support the child's or adult's need. 41 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “B” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 209 - 131LR3108(03) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
2.  Sources of fund; maximum expenditures.   All money appropriated by the State 1 
for the purposes of the fund must be deposited into the fund.  Expenditures from the fund 2 
may not exceed $100,000 in any fiscal year. 3 
3.  Rulemaking.  The department may adopt rules to implement this section.  Rules 4 
adopted pursuant to this subsection are routine technical rules as defined in Title 5, chapter 5 
375, subchapter 2-A. 6

PART YYYY 8 
Sec. YYYY-1. Department of Health and Human Services to amend rules 9 
governing education requirements for behavioral health professionals 10 
providing services for children.   No later than January 1, 2025, the Department of 11 
Health and Human Services shall amend its rule Chapter 101: MaineCare Benefits Manual, 12 
Chapter II, Section 28 and Section 65 to change the ed ucational requirements for all 13 
behavioral health professionals providing services for children, regardless of the setting in 14 
which the service is provided, and for such behavioral health professionals to receive 15 
training to provide specialized services to allow the following educational requirements: 16 
1. A minimum of 60 higher education credit hours in a related field of social services, 17 
human services, health or education; 18 
2. A minimum of 90 higher education credit hours in an unrelated field; or 19 
3. A high school diploma or equivalent with training and oversight as determined by 20 
the department in addition to the training provided for certification as a behavioral health 21 
professional. 22 
In adopting rules under this section, the Department of Health and Human Se rvices 23 
shall ensure that the training and oversight requirements for persons with a high school 24 
diploma or equivalent are consistent in both Section 28 and Section 65 of the department's 25 
rule Chapter 101: MaineCare Benefits Manual, Chapter II. 26 
The changes to educational requirements required by this Part do not affect the 27 
requirements for behavioral health professional training and the prescribed time frames. 28 
Sec. YYYY-2.  Training within existing resources.  The Department of Health 29 
and Human Services shall amend or establish contracts to train any number of additional 30 
individuals to become behavioral health professionals providing services for children 31 
pursuant to section 1, regardless of the setting in which the service is provided, within 32 
existing resources.  The department may make any changes necessary, including choosing 33 
to charge individuals or their employers fees for training, in order to offer training within 34 
existing resources. 35 
Sec. YYYY-3.  Effective date. This Part takes effect July 1, 2024. 36

Sec. ZZZZ-1.  5 MRSA §20012 is enacted to read: 38 
§20012.  Recovery Community Centers Fund 39 
The Recovery Community Centers Fund is established as a dedicated, nonlapsing fund 40 
within the Office of Behavioral Health for the purposes specified in this section.  The fund 41 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT “B” to H.P. 1420, L.D. 2214 
Page 210 - 131LR3108(03) 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
must be held separate and apart from all other money, funds and accou nts. Eligible 42 
investment earnings credited to the assets of the fund become part of the assets of the fund. 43 
Any unexpended balances remaining in the fund at the end of any fiscal year do not lapse 44 
and must be carried forward to the next fiscal year. 45 
1.  D efinitions.  As used in this section, unless the context otherwise indicates, the 5 
following terms have the following meanings. 6 
A.  "Fund" means the Recovery Community Centers Fund established in this section. 7 
B.  "Independent, nonprofit organization" means a nonprofit organization that: 8 
(1)  Operates its own agency that is a tax -exempt organization under 26 United 9 
States Code, Section 501(c)(3); or 10 
(2)  Has a fiscal agent with a fiduciary relationship between a recovery community 11 
center and another agency and: 12 
(a)  The fiscal agent is limited to managing assets and distributing funds to the 13 
recovery community center, free from conflicting self -interests, for the 14 
purpose of supporting the recovery community center's mission; 15 
(b)  The recovery community center is autonomous in its own decision making, 16 
program development, recovery services provided and advocacy efforts 17 
through the leadership of an executive board or advisory board consisting of at 18 
least 51% members who are individuals in recovery; and 19 
(c)  The fiscal agent uses no more than 4% of the revenue received from the 20 
fund for administrative purposes. 21 
C.  "Office" means the Office of Behavioral Health established in section 20011. 22 
D.  "Recovery community center" means an independent, nonprofit organizati on led 23 
and governed by representatives of local recovery communities with a primary focus 24 
on recovery from substance use disorder that provides nonclinical, peer recovery 25 
support services such as recovery support groups, recovery coaching, telephone 26 
recovery support, skill -building groups, harm reduction activities, recovery -focused 27 
outreach programs to engage people seeking recovery or in recovery and recovery -28 
focused policy and advocacy activities. 29 
2.  Sources of funds.  The State Controller shall credit to the fund:   30 
A. All money from any source, whether public or private, designated for deposit into 31 
or credited to the fund; and 32 
B. Interest earned or other investment income on balances in the fund. 33 
3.  Uses of fund.   Money credited to the fund pursuant t o subsection 2 must be 34 
expended by the office to fund recovery community centers. Money distributed from the 35 
fund must supplement, and may not supplant, the level of funding received from the State 36 
by a recovery community center in fiscal year 2022-23. 37 
4.  Application of fund to office expenses prohibited.  Money in the fund may not be 38 
applied to any expenses incurred by the office in implementing, administering or enforcing 39 
this section. 40

Sec. DDDDD -2. Administration of Infrastructure Adaptation Fund 26 
program.  Funds provided under section 7 of this Part  must be administered by the 27 
Department of Transportation and must be awarded by interagency boards using 28 
competitive processes.  The interagency boards shall allocate up to $30,000,000 of the 29 
funds provided to infrastructure projects related to wharves an d piers that support 30 
commercial fisheries and aquaculture businesses in this State and the remainder to projects 31 
related to noncoastal municipal, state or regionally significant infrastructure adaptation, 32 
repair and improvement projects that support public  safety, protection of essential 33 
community assets, regional economic needs and long-term infrastructure resiliency. Project 34 
rating criteria may include the potential extent of public safety; emergency management 35 
and infrastructure resiliency benefits; future climate conditions; ability to leverage federal 36 
and other funding; and community, economic and environmental benefits. All projects 37 
must demonstrate increased resilience to future storm and flooding impacts. The award 38 
criteria must prioritize proposals that demonstrate a significant and compelling community 39 
benefit; recipients that are not covered by Federal Emergency Management Agency 40 
disaster funds; and recipients that demonstrate that the damage is not covered by insurance 41 
and that all emergency relief currently available has been exhausted. The administration of 42 
the funds must include sufficient documentation and record -keeping requirements to 43 
provide assurance that funds have been awarded consistent with the program guidelines 44 
and used for the intended purpose. 45

CHAPTER 154 7 
MUNICIPAL EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICES 8 
§3171.  Definitions 9 
As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise indicates, the following terms 10 
have the following meanings. 11 
1.  Ambulance service.   "Ambulance service" has the same meaning as in Title 32, 12 
section 83, subsection 5. 13 
2.  Transporting emergency medical services.   "Transporting emergency medical 14 
services" means emergency medical services provided by an ambulance service. 15 
§3172.  Municipal emergency medical services 16 
1.  Adoption of plan.   The municipal officers of a municipality may adopt a plan 17 
stipulating the method by which transporting emergency medical services will be delivered 18 
within the municipality.  A municipality that elects to adopt such a plan is not required 19 
under this subsection to directly or indirectly provide or fund the delivery of transporting 20 
emergency medical services within the municipality.  The municipal officers may as 21 
necessary amend a plan adopted pursuant to this subsection. 22 
2.  Posting and submission of plan.   If a municipality adopts or amends a plan 23 
pursuant to subsection 1, the municipal officers shall ensure that the plan is posted in the 24 
same manner as ordinances are posted and shall submit the plan or amended plan for the 25 
purpose of collecting data to the Department of Public Safety, Maine Emergency Medical 26 
Services and the Maine Emergency Medical Services Commission established in Title 32, 27 
section 99, subsection 1. 28

term must be filled through an appointment by the appointing authority for the vacant seat. 13 
5.  Quorum.  A quorum of the commission consists of 14 members. 14

as soon as all appointments are made and to the extent resources are available.  At the first 16

among its members.  The commission may select new officers annually. 18 
7.  Meetings.  The commission may meet as often as necessary but must meet at least 19 
quarterly.  A meeting may be called by the chair or by any 4 members.  The commission 20 
shall take and maintain minutes of all meetings. 21

as needed.   23

out its duties. 25

and resources, including recommendations for improvements, new programs and 39 
initiatives and funding options for oversight and administration of the State's 40 
emergency medical services system;   41

Sec. FFFFF -6.  Recruitment and retention adjustment task force.   The 24 
Department of Administrative and Financial Services, Bureau of Human Resources shall 25 
convene a task force mediated by a neutral 3rd party to review and make recommendations 26 
regarding the criteria required under the Maine Revised Statutes, Title 5, se ction 7065, 27 
subsection 2-D for a recruitment and retention adjustment to be authorized. The task force 28 
must consist of one member from each of the 8 bargaining units of the executive branch, 29 
appointed by each unit's respective bargaining agent, and up to 8  additional members, 30 
appointed by the Governor. The task force must be cochaired by one member representing 31 
the State and one bargaining unit representative.  The cochairs must be selected by the 32 
membership of the task force. A state employee appointed to serve on the task force may 33 
participate in the work of the task force during the employee's regular working hours 34 
without loss of pay or benefits.  By November 30, 2024, the task force shall complete the 35 
review and submit recommendations to the Department of Administrative and Financial 36 
Services, including draft legislation necessary to implement any proposed changes to the 37 
criteria for a recruitment and retention adjustment that are supported by a majority of the 38 
task force membership, and the department s hall submit that proposed legislation to the 39 
First Regular Session of the 132nd Legislature. The task force shall meet once per month 40 
or as necessary to complete its work. 41

SUMMARY 1 
PART A 2 
This Part makes appropriations and allocations of funds for fiscal year  2023-24 and 3 
fiscal year 2024-25. 4 
PART B 5 
This Part makes appropriations and allocations of funds for approved reclassifications 6 
and range changes. 7 
PART C 8 
This Part establishes the total cost of education from kindergarten to grade 12, the state 9 
contribution and the mill expectation for the local contribution for fiscal year 2024-25. 10 
PART D 11 
This Part authorizes the transfer of Federal Expenditures Fund - ARP State Fiscal 12 
Recovery funds within or between departments or agencies during fiscal years 2023 -24, 13 
2024-25 and 2025-26. 14 
Additionally, this Part allows limited -period positions funded with Federal 15 
Expenditures Fund - ARP State Fiscal Recovery funds to be extended through December 16 
31, 2026. 17 
This Part also allocates one -time funding of $10,000,000 in fiscal year 2024 -25 to 18 
complete projects initially funded with funds received through the federal American 19 
Rescue Plan Act of 2021. 20 
PART E 21 
This Part specifies that fees for the examination of plans  or specifications for new or 22 
altered elevators and tramways are not subject to a $500 cap applied to other fees related 23 
to elevator inspections.  It also provides that fees for  the examination of plans  and 24 
specifications may not exceed 1.5% of the cost of the new or altered elevator or tramway.  25 
Finally, this Part directs the Director of the Office of Professional and Occupational 26 
Regulation within the Department of Professional and Financial Regulation to amend rules 27 
to change fees associated with elevator inspections to cover the costs of additional Elevator 28 
Inspector positions and to allow for future reclassification or reorganization of all Elevator 29 
Inspector positions. The director is required to report to the  joint standing committee or 30 
joint select committee of the Legislature  having jurisdiction over housing matters as to 31 
whether the fee changes are sufficient to add the positions at a more competitive 32 
compensation level. 33 
PART F 34 
This Part updates the definition of "biennial base year appropriation " for the laws 35 
governing the General Fund appropriation limitation and clarifies that when the Maine 36 
Budget Stabilization Fund is at its statutory limit funds transferred from the General Fund 37 
to the Irrevocable Trust Funds for Other Post -employment Benefits are for the trust fund 38 
established for the state employee retiree health plan. 39 
This Part also increases the biennial base year appropriation, for fiscal year 2024 -25 40 
only, to 99% of the baseline General Fund revenue. 41

COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
PART H 1 
This Part, beginning January 1, 2025, makes the following changes to the sales and use 2 
tax and service provider tax provisions: 3 
1.  Amends Maine sales and use tax law to move from the current imposition of sales 4 
and use tax on the lessor upfront on the full value of its rental property when purchased and 5 
used in Maine through leasing to instead requiring the lessor to collect sales and use tax 6 
due from the lessee on each periodic rental payment; 7 
2.  Provides a limited refund period and claim process for sales and use tax previously 8 
paid by qualified lessors on its rental property stock; 9 
3.  Relocates the taxable services and related provisions under the service provider tax 10 
to the sales tax and its accompanying 5.5% rate; and repeals the service provider tax; 11 
4.  Provides a sales and use tax exemption for purchases by nonprofit entities that have 12 
been determined by the United States Internal Revenue Service to be exempt from federal 13 
income taxation under Section 501(c)(3) of the Code; and 14 
5.  Provides a broader sales and use tax exemption for durable medical equipment and 15 
breast pumps sold or leased for home use and for mobility enhancing equipment sold or 16 
leased for use in a home or motor vehicle. 17 
PART I 18 
This Part requires the State Controller to carry forward up to $750,000 of unexpended 19 
balance in the Capital Expenditures line category in  the Department of Agriculture, 20 
Conservation and Forestry, Bureau of Agriculture program, General Fund account the end 21 
of fiscal year 2023-24 to upgrade the Cony Road facility in Augusta. 22 
PART J 23 
This Part transfers $750,000 from the unappropriated surplus of the General Fund to 24 
the Bureau of Agriculture program, Other Special Revenue Funds account within the 25 
Department of Agriculture, Conservation and Forestry to be used to renovate the office 26 
area of the Cony Road facility in Augusta. 27 
PART K 28 
This Part requires a one-time transfer in fiscal year 2024 -25 of all funds in excess of 29 
$200,000 of unencumbered balance forward in the Personal Services line category and in 30 
excess of $300,000 of unencumbered balance forward in the All Other line category in the 31 
Department of Agriculture, Conservation and Forestry, Division of Forest Protection, 32 
General Fund account to the Capital Expenditures line category in the Department of 33 
Agriculture, Conservation and Forestry, Division of Forest Protection, General Fund 34 
account. 35

This Part establishes as units within the Land for Maine's Future Trust Fund 5 units: 1 
the Public Access to Maine Waters Fund; the Maine Working Waterfront Access Protection 2

PART N 7 
This Part creates the Maine Mass Violence Care Fund in the Department of the 8 
Attorney General to provide financial support to victims of mass violence crimes and their 9 
families and household members.  The financial support is for out -of-pocket costs for 10 
physical and behavioral health  care not otherwise paid for by insurance or some other 11 
source.  The Treasurer of State is directed to administer the fund in a manner consistent 12 
with investment standards established in the Maine Uniform Trust Code. 13 
When the underlying crime is a mass violence crime, payments may be made from the 14 
existing Victims' Compensation Fund but all payments in excess of the $15,000 limit on 15 
payments from the Victims' Compensation Fund must be made from the Maine Mass 16 
Violence Care Fund. 17 
The Maine Mass Violence Care  Fund is funded by an initial transfer of $5,000,000 18 
from the General Fund unappropriated surplus.  Disbursements from the fund are made by 19 
the Victims' Compensation Board within the Department of the Attorney General but may 20 
only be from the earnings on the fund or from donations to the fund. 21 
This Part also creates a working group to recommend changes to eligibility standards 22 
with regard to distributions from the fund as established by the Victims' Compensation 23 
Board. 24 
PART O 25 
This Part requir es the transfer of $4,800,000 in fiscal year 2024 -25 from the 26 
unappropriated surplus of the General Fund to the Department of Corrections, 27 
Administration - Corrections, Other Special Revenue Funds account for the purpose of 28 
supporting the one-time implementation costs of the offender management system. 29 
PART P 30 
This Part requires the State Controller to carry forward up to $900,000 appropriated in 31 
Part A for the subscription costs for the offender management system used by the 32 
Department of Corrections. 33 
PART Q 34 
This Part changes the maximum amount of funding that may be held in the Disaster 35 
Recovery Fund to address the existing obligations of the fund and plan for the increasing 36 
frequency of disaster declarations. The Part removes the Consumer Price Index factor from 37 
the statute governing the fund. The Part also transfers $15,000,000 from the unappropriated 38 
surplus of the General Fund to the Disaster Recovery Fund, Other Special Revenue Funds 39 
account within the Department of Defense, Veterans and Emergency Management to fund 40 
the State’s share of estimated disaster recovery costs. 41
